\doxysubsection{详细描述}
\subsubsection*{template$<$typename Derived$>$\newline
class Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base$<$ Derived $>$}
\doxylink{class_base}{Base} class for all 1D and 2D array, and related expressions 

An array is similar to a dense vector or matrix. While matrices are mathematical objects with well defined linear algebra operators, an array is just a collection of scalar values arranged in a one or two dimensionnal fashion. As the main consequence, all operations applied to an array are performed coefficient wise. Furthermore, arrays support scalar math functions of the c++ standard library (e.\+g., std\+::sin(x)), and convenient constructors allowing to easily write generic code working for both scalar values and arrays.

This class is the base that is inherited by all array expression types.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{模板参数}
{\em Derived} & is the derived type, e.\+g., an array or an expression type.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
This class can be extended with the help of the plugin mechanism described on the page \doxylink{TopicCustomizing_Plugins}{Extending Matrix\+Base (and other classes)} by defining the preprocessor symbol {\ttfamily EIGEN\+\_\+\+ARRAYBASE\+\_\+\+PLUGIN}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{参见}
class \doxylink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix_base}{Matrix\+Base}, \doxylink{TopicClassHierarchy}{The class hierarchy} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{返回}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise == operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{警告}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{class_eigen_1_1_dense_base_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and \doxylink{class_eigen_1_1_dense_base_acc982903f94ed372fafa901e6822ae8d}{is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than()}.

\end{DoxyReturn}
\textbackslash{}specialfunctions\+\_\+module

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\+: 
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}


\begin{DoxyNote}{注解}
This function supports only float and double scalar types in c++11 mode. To support other scalar types, or float/double in non c++11 mode, the user has to provide implementations of lgamma(\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_eigen_1_1_array_base_a438640146f3e7488f09a4f60c305b1d9} 
template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base_ae288968798661f74b36fe7a3c4341ef4}{Log1p\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::log1p (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{返回}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise logarithm of 1 plus {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
In exact arithmetic, {\ttfamily x.\+log()} is equivalent to {\ttfamily }(x+1).\doxylink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base_a7748ba1f6891fa4e10723a8bf77b8770}{log()}, however, with finite precision, this function is much more accurate when {\ttfamily x} is close to zero.

EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC Derived \& \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_dense_base}{Eigen\+::\+Dense\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::operator= (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_eigen_1_1_eigen_base}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Copies the generic expression {\itshape other} into \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this. 

The expression must provide a (templated) eval\+To(\+Derived\& dst) const function which does the actual job. In practice, this allows any user to write its own special matrix without having to modify \doxylink{class_eigen_1_1_matrix_base}{Matrix\+Base}

a reference to \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{返回}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise == operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{警告}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{class_eigen_1_1_dense_base_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and \doxylink{class_eigen_1_1_dense_base_acc982903f94ed372fafa901e6822ae8d}{is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than()}.
\end{DoxyWarning}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{zeta()}{zeta()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_eigen_1_1_array_base_ad996aade2210f810f1b11d43a611b1e3} 
template$<$typename Derived$>$ \\
template$<$typename DerivedQ$>$ \\
const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_cwise_binary_op}{Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_eigen_1_1internal_1_1scalar__zeta__op}{internal\+::scalar\+\_\+zeta\+\_\+op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base_a9d10903d33b230df8226b2adc0179c41}{Scalar}} $>$, const Derived, const DerivedQ $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_eigen_1_1_array_base}{Eigen\+::\+Array\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::zeta (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{_array_base_8h_a140b988ffa480af0799d873ce22898f2}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+CURRENT\+\_\+\+STORAGE\+\_\+\+BASE\+\_\+\+CLASS}}$<$ DerivedQ $>$ \&}]{q}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{返回}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise zeta function.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\textbackslash{}specialfunctions\+\_\+module

It returns the Riemann zeta function of two arguments {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and {\itshape q\+:} 


\begin{DoxyParams}{参数}
{\em \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} & is the exposent, it must be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 1 \\
\hline
{\em q} & is the shift, it must be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 0\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{注解}
This function supports only float and double scalar types. To support other scalar types, the user has to provide implementations of zeta(\+T,\+T) for any scalar type T to be supported.
\end{DoxyNote}
This method is an alias for zeta(\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this,q);

\end{DoxySeeAlso}
